data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_Norway" title="Template:Politics of Norway"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_Norway" title="Template talk:Politics of Norway"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:Politics_of_Norway" title="Special:EditPage/Template:Politics of Norway"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table><figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Norway_municipalities_2020_blank.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Norway_municipalities_2020_blank.svg/200px-Norway_municipalities_2020_blank.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="283" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Norway_municipalities_2020_blank.svg/300px-Norway_municipalities_2020_blank.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Norway_municipalities_2020_blank.svg/400px-Norway_municipalities_2020_blank.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2105" data-file-height="2980" /></a><figcaption>Map of municipalities (2020)</figcaption></figure><p><a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> is divided into 11 administrative regions, called <a href="/wiki/County" title="County">counties</a> (<span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">fylker</i></span> in Norwegian, singular: <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">fylke</i></span>), and 357 <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipalities</a> (<i>kommuner/-ar</i>, singular: <i>kommune</i> – cf. <a href="/wiki/Municipality#communes" title="Municipality">communes</a>). The capital city <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a> is considered both a county and a municipality.</p><p>Municipalities are the atomic unit of local government in Norway and are responsible for primary education (until 10th grade), outpatient health services, senior citizen services, unemployment and other social services, zoning, economic development, and municipal roads. Law enforcement and <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Norway" title="Church of Norway">church services</a> are provided at a national level in Norway.</p><p>Municipalities are undergoing continuous consolidation. In 1930, there were 747 municipalities in Norway. As of 2020 there are 356 municipalities, a reduction from 422. See the <a href="/wiki/List_of_former_municipalities_of_Norway" title="List of former municipalities of Norway">list of former municipalities of Norway</a> for further detail about municipal mergers.</p><p>The consolidation effort is complicated by a number of factors. Since block grants are made by the national government to the municipalities based on an assessment of need, there is little incentive for the municipalities to lose local autonomy. The national policy is that municipalities should only merge voluntarily, and studies are underway to identify potential gains.</p><meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" /><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_municipalities_of_Norway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Terminology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2><p>The Norwegian word <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">kommune</i></span> is loaned from the French <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">commune</i></span>, which ultimately derives from Latin <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">communia</i></span>, <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">communis</i></span> ("common").<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kven_language" title="Kven language">Kven</a> equivalent is <span title="Kven-language text"><i lang="fkv">kommuuni</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Northern_S%C3%A1mi" title="Northern Sámi">Northern Sámi</a>, there are two words for a municipality: <span title="Northern Sami-language text"><i lang="se">suohkan</i></span> and <span title="Northern Sami-language text"><i lang="se">gielda</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Both are loan words from Scandinavian languages, the first of which is related to the Norwegian words <a href="/wiki/Socken" title="Socken">sokn and sogn</a> (a parish).<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The second term is related to the Norwegian word <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">gjeld</i></span> (<a href="/wiki/Prestegjeld" title="Prestegjeld">prestegjeld</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lule_S%C3%A1mi" title="Lule Sámi">Lule Sámi</a> likewise has two words for municipalities: <span title="Lule Sami-language text"><i lang="smj">suohkan</i></span> and <span title="Lule Sami-language text"><i lang="smj">giellda</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Southern_S%C3%A1mi" title="Southern Sámi">Southern Sámi</a> word is <span title="Southern Sami-language text"><i lang="sma">tjïelte</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></p><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_municipalities_of_Norway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Administration"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2><p>Each <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipality</a> has its own governmental leaders: the <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a> (<i>ordfører</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_council#Norway" title="Municipal council">municipal council</a> (<i>kommunestyre</i>). The mayor is the executive leader. The municipal council is the deliberative and <a href="/wiki/Organs_of_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Organs of state">legislative body</a> of the municipality and it is the highest governing body in the municipality. The members of the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_council#Norway" title="Municipal council">municipal council</a> are elected for a 4-year <a href="/wiki/Term_of_office" title="Term of office">term</a>. A subdivision of the full council is the executive council (<i>formannskap</i>), composed of 5 members.  </p><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">Municipalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_municipalities_of_Norway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section:
